    Palatal nasal
   </h1>

      <table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width: 16em;">
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;background: #f2f2ce;">
         Alveolo-palatal nasal
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background: #ffffe6;">
         <span style="font-size: 5em; line-height: 1.2em; vertical-align: super; font-weight: normal;">
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           n̠ʲ
          </span>
         </span>
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background: #ffffe6;">
         <span style="font-size: 5em; line-height: 1.2em; vertical-align: super; font-weight: normal;">
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           ɲ̟
          </span>
         </span>
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;background: #ffffe6;">
         <span style="font-size: 5em; line-height: 1.2em; vertical-align: super; font-weight: normal;">
          <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
           ȵ
          </span>
         </span>
        </th>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The
       <b>
        palatal nasal
       </b>
       is a type of
       <a href="/wiki/Consonant" title="Consonant">
        consonant
       </a>
       , used in some
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Speech_communication" title="Speech communication">
        spoken
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Language" title="Language">
        languages
       </a>
       . The symbol in the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
        International Phonetic Alphabet
       </a>
       that represents this sound is ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/%C6%9D" title="Ɲ">
         ɲ
        </a>
       </span>
       ⟩,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELadefoged2005xviii_1-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELadefoged2005xviii-1">
         [1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       a lowercase letter
       <i>
        n
       </i>
       with a leftward-pointing tail protruding from the bottom of the left stem of the letter. The equivalent
       <a href="/wiki/X-SAMPA" title="X-SAMPA">
        X-SAMPA
       </a>
       symbol is
       <code>
        J
       </code>
       . The IPA symbol ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        ɲ
       </span>
       ⟩ is similar to ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        ɳ
       </span>
       ⟩, the symbol for the
       <a href="/wiki/Retroflex_nasal" title="Retroflex nasal">
        retroflex nasal
       </a>
       , which has a rightward-pointing hook extending from the bottom of the right stem, and to ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        ŋ
       </span>
       ⟩, the symbol for the
       <a href="/wiki/Velar_nasal" title="Velar nasal">
        velar nasal
       </a>
       , which has a leftward-pointing hook extending from the bottom of the right stem; the symbol was derived from a
       <a href="/wiki/Typographic_ligature" title="Typographic ligature">
        ligature
       </a>
       of
       <i>
        gn
       </i>
       , which represents the sound in French and Italian.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Palatal nasals are more common than the palatal stops
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        [
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_palatal_stop#Palatal_or_alveolo-palatal" title="Voiceless palatal stop">
          c
         </a>
        </span>
        ,
        <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
         <a href="/wiki/Voiced_palatal_stop#Palatal_or_alveolo-palatal" title="Voiced palatal stop">
          ɟ
         </a>
        </span>
        ]
       </span>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELadefoged2005163_3-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELadefoged2005163-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">
        Spanish
       </a>
       and languages whose writing systems are influenced by
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_orthography" title="Spanish orthography">
        Spanish orthography
       </a>
       , this sound is represented with the letter
       <i>
        eñe
       </i>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/%C3%91" title="Ñ">
        ñ
       </a>
       ); the same is true for
       <a href="/wiki/Occitan_language" title="Occitan language">
        Occitan
       </a>
       , the source of the
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">
        Portuguese
       </a>
       digraph
       <i>
        ene-agá
       </i>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Nh_(digraph)" title="Nh (digraph)">
        nh
       </a>
       ), used by languages whose writing systems are influenced by
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_orthography" title="Portuguese orthography">
        Portuguese orthography
       </a>
       , such as
       <a href="/wiki/Vietnamese_language" title="Vietnamese language">
        Vietnamese
       </a>
       ; in
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">
        Catalan
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">
        Hungarian
       </a>
       and many African languages, as
       <a href="/wiki/Swahili_language" title="Swahili language">
        Swahili
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Dinka_language" title="Dinka language">
        Dinka
       </a>
       , the digraph
       <a href="/wiki/Ny_(digraph)" title="Ny (digraph)">
        <i>
         ny
        </i>
       </a>
       is used, in Italian and French
       <i>
        gn
       </i>
       is used .
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <b>
        alveolo-palatal nasal
       </b>
       is a type of
       <a href="/wiki/Consonant" title="Consonant">
        consonantal
       </a>
       sound, used in some
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oral_language" title="Oral language">
        oral languages
       </a>
       . There is no dedicated symbol in the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Phonetic_Alphabet" title="International Phonetic Alphabet">
        International Phonetic Alphabet
       </a>
       that represents this sound. If more precision is desired, it may be transcribed ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        n̠ʲ
       </span>
       ⟩ or ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        ɲ̟
       </span>
       ⟩; these are essentially equivalent, since the contact includes both the blade and body (but not the tip) of the tongue. There is a non-IPA letter ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        ȵ
       </span>
       ⟩ ("n", plus the curl found in the symbols for alveolo-palatal sibilant fricatives ⟨
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Voiceless_alveolo-palatal_fricative" title="Voiceless alveolo-palatal fricative">
         ɕ
        </a>
       </span>
       ,
       <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
        <a href="/wiki/Voiced_alveolo-palatal_fricative" title="Voiced alveolo-palatal fricative">
         ʑ
        </a>
       </span>
       ⟩), used especially in Sinological circles.
      </p>
      <p>
       The alveolo-palatal nasal is commonly described as palatal; it is often unclear whether a language has a true palatal or not. Many languages claimed to have a palatal nasal, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_language" title="Portuguese language">
        Portuguese
       </a>
       , actually have an
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alveolo-palatal_nasal" title="Alveolo-palatal nasal">
        alveolo-palatal nasal
       </a>
       . This is likely true of several of the languages listed here. Some dialects of
       <a href="/wiki/Irish_language" title="Irish language">
        Irish
       </a>
       as well as some non-standard dialects of
       <a href="/wiki/Malayalam" title="Malayalam">
        Malayalam
       </a>
       are reported to contrast alveolo-palatal and palatal nasals.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTENí_Chasaide1999_4-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTENí_Chasaide1999-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELadefogedMaddieson199633_5-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELadefogedMaddieson199633-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       There is also a
       <b>
        post-palatal nasal
       </b>
       (also called
       <b>
        pre-velar
       </b>
       ,
       <b>
        fronted velar
       </b>
       etc.) in some languages.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Features">
        Features
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Palatal_nasal&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Features">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Features of the voiced palatal nasal:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Manner_of_articulation" title="Manner of articulation">
         manner of articulation
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Occlusive" title="Occlusive">
         occlusive
        </a>
        , which means it is produced by obstructing airflow in the vocal tract. Because the consonant is also
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nasal_stop" title="Nasal stop">
         nasal
        </a>
        , the blocked airflow is redirected through the nose.
       </li>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Place_of_articulation" title="Place of articulation">
         place of articulation
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Palatal_consonant" title="Palatal consonant">
         palatal
        </a>
        , which means it is articulated with the middle or back part of the
        <a href="/wiki/Tongue" title="Tongue">
         tongue
        </a>
        raised to the
        <a href="/wiki/Hard_palate" title="Hard palate">
         hard palate
        </a>
        .
       </li>
       <li>
        Its
        <a href="/wiki/Phonation" title="Phonation">
         phonation
        </a>
        is voiced, which means the vocal cords vibrate during the articulation.
       </li>
       <li>
        It is a nasal consonant, which means air is allowed to escape through the nose, either exclusively (
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nasal_stop" title="Nasal stop">
         nasal stops
        </a>
        ) or in addition to through the mouth.
       </li>
       <li>
        Because the sound is not produced with airflow over the tongue, the
        <a href="/wiki/Central_consonant" title="Central consonant">
         central
        </a>
        –
        <a href="/wiki/Lateral_consonant" title="Lateral consonant">
         lateral
        </a>
        dichotomy does not apply.
       </li>
       <li>
        The
        <a href="/wiki/Airstream_mechanism" title="Airstream mechanism">
         airstream mechanism
        </a>
        is
        <a href="/wiki/Egressive_sound" title="Egressive sound">
         pulmonic
        </a>
        , which means it is articulated by pushing air solely with the
        <a href="/wiki/Lung" title="Lung">
         lungs
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Thoracic_diaphragm" title="Thoracic diaphragm">
         diaphragm
        </a>
        , as in most sounds.
       </li>
      </ul>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Occurrence">

       </span>

        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

          </a>
          ]
         </span>
         in standard Romanian. See

        <li id="cite_note-FOOTNOTEAragão2009168-25">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-FOOTNOTEAragão2009168_25-0">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>

        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-26">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-26">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <a href="#CITEREFCagliari1974">
           Cagliari 1974
          </a>
          , p. 77.
          <b>
           Citation:
          </b>
          <i>
           Em português, o
           <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
            [ɲ]
           </span>
           se aproxima mais do
           <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
            [
            <a href="/wiki/Velar_nasal" title="Velar nasal">
             ŋ
            </a>
            ]
           </span>
           do que do
           <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
            [
            <a href="/wiki/Dental,_alveolar_and_postalveolar_nasals#Dental_or_denti-alveolar" title="Dental, alveolar and postalveolar nasals">
             n
            </a>
            ]
           </span>
           ; por isso será classificado como "central" e não como pré-palatal. O
           <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
            [
            <a href="/wiki/Palatal_lateral_approximant" title="Palatal lateral approximant">
             ʎ
            </a>
            ]
           </span>
           em muitas línguas se realiza como "central"; em português,
           <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
            [
            <a href="/wiki/Palatal_lateral_approximant" title="Palatal lateral approximant">
             ʎ
            </a>
            ]
           </span>
           tende a
           <span class="IPA" title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)">
            [lj]
           </span>
           e se realiza sempre na região prepalatal.
          </i>
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-vinho-27">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">

           Portuguese vinho: diachronic evidence for biphonemic nasal vowels
          </a>
         </span>
        </li>

                       <div class="hlist navbar" style="float: right;">
                        <ul>
                         <li>

                          </a>
                         </li>

                           full chart
                          </a>

                           template
                          </a>
                         </li>
                        </ul>
                       </div>
                       <p>
                        Where symbols appear in pairs, the leftmost represents a
                        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiceless_consonant" title="Voiceless consonant">
                         voiceless consonant
                        </a>
                        , and the rightmost represents a
                        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Voiced_consonant" title="Voiced consonant">
                         voiced consonant
                        </a>
                        .
                       </p>
                       <p>
                        Shaded areas denote articulations judged to be impossible.
